### Post by gmclella on 2009-08-23
Ok, so I've tried to enable the desktop effects and when I do it says that the Desktop Effects could not be enabled.    I have an old ATI Radeon 7200 and from what I've read on the Radeon Driver page at help.ubuntu.com/community/RadeonDriver it seems to be supported.    I'm hoping someone can help me out.

Here's some info:
lspci -nn | grep VGA
```
01:00.0 VGA compatible controller [0300]: ATI Technologies Inc Radeon R100 QD [Radeon 7200] [1002:5144]

```glxinfo | grep vendor
```
server glx vendor string: SGI
client glx vendor string: SGI
OpenGL vendor string: Tungsten Graphics, Inc.

```I've edited my config file as follows:
```
# xorg.conf (X.Org X Window System server configuration file)
#
# This file was generated by dexconf, the Debian X Configuration tool, using
# values from the debconf database.
#
# Edit this file with caution, and see the xorg.conf manual page.
# (Type "man xorg.conf" at the shell prompt.)

Have you gone into System/Administration/Hardware Drivers?

That's the first place I'd look for an updated driver. If not, check ATI's website.

### Post by gmclella on 2009-08-23
Doesn't that enable a proprietary driver?  The Radeon help pages says:
***If you previously used the proprietary "fglrx" driver it is highly recommended to totally get rid of the fglrx package: ***

When I brought it up there were no proprietary drivers are in use on this system and there were no boxes to check either.  The list was completely empty.

---

### Post by oboedad55 on 2009-08-23
> **gmclella said:**
> Doesn't that enable a proprietary driver?  The Radeon help pages says:
***If you previously used the proprietary "fglrx" driver it is highly recommended to totally get rid of the fglrx package: ***

When I brought it up there were no proprietary drivers are in use on this system and there were no boxes to check either.  The list was completely empty.

I checked ATI's web site for you. I don't see a Linux driver is available from them. That doesn't mean there is not one, I just couldn't find  it.

Jon

---

### Post by krazyd on 2009-08-24
Don't install the proprietary fglrx drivers. Your card is supported by the open source drivers which you're already using.

Try this: [http://wiki.compiz-fusion.org/Hardware/ATI](http://wiki.compiz-fusion.org/Hardware/ATI)

also can you paste the content of /var/log/Xorg.0.log

---
